2:28:1783:0:14:72:454:700:12:Times:12:Times:C:Financial Crises, Dollarization, and Lending of Last Resort in Open Economies
2:29:1860:14:14:72:241:686:12:Times:12:Times:C:Luigi Bocola and Guido Lorenzoni
2:30:1892:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:C:NBER Working Paper No. 23984
2:31:1920:14:14:72:150:658:12:Times:12:Times:C:November 2017
2:32:1933:14:28:72:225:644:12:Times:12:Times:C:JEL No. E44,F34,F41,G11,G15
2:33:1960:28:28:306:339:616:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:34:1968:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:C:Foreign currency borrowing is perceived as a source of financial instability in emerging markets. We
2:35:2068:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:C:propose a theory where liability dollarization arises from an insurance motive of domestic savers. Because
2:36:2174:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:C:financial crises are associated with currency depreciations, savers are reluctant to hold assets denominated
2:37:2282:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:C:in local currency. This behavior makes local currency debt expensive, incentivizing borrowers to issue
2:38:2384:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:C:foreign currency debt. We show that this mechanism can generate multiple equilibria, with the bad
2:39:2481:14:14:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:C:equilibrium characterized by dollarization and financial instability. A domestic lender of last resort
2:40:2583:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:C:can eliminate the bad equilibrium, but interventions need to be fiscally credible. Holdings of foreign
2:41:2685:14:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:C:currency reserves hedge the fiscal position of the government and enhance its credibility, thus improving
2:42:2790:14:42:72:159:476:12:Times:12:Times:C:financial stability.
2:43:2810:42:14:72:135:434:12:Times:12:Times:C:Luigi Bocola
2:44:2822:14:14:72:198:420:12:Times:12:Times:C:Department of Economics
2:45:2845:14:14:72:191:406:12:Times:12:Times:C:Northwestern University
2:46:2868:14:14:72:170:392:12:Times:12:Times:C:2001 Sheridan Road
2:47:2886:14:14:72:167:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:Evanston, IL 60208
2:48:2904:14:14:72:124:364:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:49:2912:14:28:72:223:350:12:Times:12:Times:C:luigi.bocola@northwestern.edu
2:50:2941:28:14:72:154:322:12:Times:12:Times:C:Guido Lorenzoni
2:51:2956:14:14:72:198:308:12:Times:12:Times:C:Department of Economics
2:52:2979:14:14:72:191:294:12:Times:12:Times:C:Northwestern University
2:53:3002:14:14:72:154:280:12:Times:12:Times:C:2211 Campus Dr
2:54:3016:14:14:72:167:266:12:Times:12:Times:C:Evanston, IL 60208
2:55:3034:14:14:72:124:252:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:56:3042:14:0:72:242:238:12:Times:12:Times:C:guido.lorenzoni@northwestern.edu
3:57:3074:0:33:56:181:735:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:1    Introduction
3:58:3091:33:19:56:538:702:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Emerging  economies  are  exposed  to  recurrent  episodes  of  financial  instability.   At  least
3:59:3190:19:18:56:538:683:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:since the East Asian crisis of 1997, this instability has been linked to the presence of debt
3:60:3283:18:18:56:538:665:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:denominated  in  foreign  currency  issued  by  banks,  firms,  or  households.   These  various
3:61:3379:18:18:56:538:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:forms of liability dollarization can amplify the effects of financial crises, as crises are typ-
3:62:3475:18:18:56:538:629:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ically associated with currency depreciations,  and depreciations increase the real burden
3:63:3565:18:18:56:538:611:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  foreign  currency  debt.   Liability  dollarization  also  makes  it  challenging  for  domestic
3:64:3665:18:18:56:538:593:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:authorities to intervene in financial markets when a crisis takes place:  covering the losses
3:65:3758:18:18:56:538:575:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of local borrowers by expanding domestic money supply can lead to inflationary concerns
3:66:3845:18:18:56:538:557:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and exacerbate the currency depreciation, while using government borrowing may lead to
3:67:3931:18:21:56:277:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:concerns about public debt sustainability.
3:68:3973:21:18:70:538:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:While we have a good understanding of the mechanisms by which foreign currency debt
3:69:4056:18:18:56:538:500:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:makes emerging economies more fragile, we still have a relatively limited understanding
3:70:4143:18:18:56:538:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the incentives that drive the accumulation of foreign currency debt in the first place.  In
3:71:4237:18:18:56:538:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this paper we build a theory of liability dollarization and study how it interacts with policy
3:72:4331:18:21:56:454:446:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interventions, focusing in particular on operations of lending of last resort.
3:73:4409:21:18:70:538:425:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our theory builds on two observations emphasized in recent empirical work. First, coun-
3:74:4496:18:18:56:538:407:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tries characterized by high levels of liability dollarization are also countries where domestic
3:75:4591:18:18:56:538:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:agents tend to save in foreign currency.1Second, local currency bonds in these economies
3:76:4679:18:18:56:538:371:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are  characterized  by  positive  excess  returns  over  comparable  dollar  bonds,  which  effec-
3:77:4777:18:18:56:538:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tively means that borrowing in dollars is cheaper than borrowing in local currency.2In our
3:78:4867:18:18:56:538:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:theory, both facts are driven by the incentives of domestic savers to insure against a crisis.
3:79:4961:18:18:56:538:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Because crises are associated with a depreciation of the local currency, domestic savers are
3:80:5053:18:19:56:538:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reluctant to hold local currency assets.  This behavior puts upward pressure on local cur-
3:81:5143:19:18:56:538:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rency interest rates, incentivizing domestic borrowers to issue debt in foreign currency. We
3:82:5235:18:18:56:538:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:show that this mechanism can lead to multiple equilibria, with a bad equilibrium charac-
3:83:5323:18:18:56:538:244:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:terized by higher excess returns on domestic currency bonds, more financial dollarization,
3:84:5413:18:18:56:538:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  a  higher  probability  of  crises.   In  line  with  this  logic,  and  in  contrast  with  the  con-
3:85:5520:18:18:56:538:208:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ventional view, we also show that ex-post government interventions that reduce financial
3:86:5608:18:18:56:538:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:instability can induce the private sector to take safer choices ex ante:  by reducing savers’
3:87:5701:18:19:56:538:172:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:demand for insurance, they can lead in equilibrium to lower levels of liability dollarization.
3:88:5795:19:16:73:538:153:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:1This correlation is documented inDe Nicoló, Honohan, and Ize(2003) andLevy-Yeyati(2006).Arteta
3:89:5890:16:9:56:453:137:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:(2005) shows that this relation is stronger for countries with more volatile exchange rates.
3:90:5982:9:15:73:538:128:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:2Burnside,  Eichenbaum,  and  Rebelo(2007)  first  documented  large  deviations  from  uncovered  interest
3:91:6089:15:12:56:538:113:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:rate parity (UIP) for emerging market bonds.  Recent work byDalgic(2017) andWiriadinata(2017) finds a
3:92:6190:12:0:56:529:101:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:positive correlation across countries between these UIP deviations and the degree of liability dollarization.
4:93:6300:0:18:70:538:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We develop these arguments in a framework that extends a “third-generation” currency
4:94:6384:18:18:56:538:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:crisis model (Krugman, 1999) by adding an explicit treatment of ex ante portfolio decisions
4:95:6475:18:18:56:538:700:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of borrowers and savers, in line with recent developments in the macro-financial literature
4:96:6566:18:18:56:538:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(Gertler  and  Kiyotaki,  2010;  Brunnermeier  and  Sannikov,  2014;  He  and  Krishnamurthy,
4:97:6659:18:18:56:538:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2015). We consider a small open economy populated by two types of domestic agents, con-
4:98:6746:18:18:56:538:646:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sumers and bankers, and by risk-neutral foreign investors.  Consumers work for domestic
4:99:6833:18:19:56:538:628:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:firms and save in bonds denominated in domestic and foreign currency. Bankers borrow in
4:100:6920:19:18:56:538:609:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:domestic and foreign currency and use these resources along with their accumulated net
4:101:7006:18:18:56:538:591:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:worth to purchase domestic capital, which is used as input in production.  The model fea-
4:102:7095:18:18:56:538:573:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tures two sources of financial frictions: banks face a potentially binding financial constraint,
4:103:7191:18:21:56:396:555:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and foreign investors only borrow and lend in foreign currency.
4:104:7254:21:18:70:538:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our economy is exposed to self-fulfilling crises because of a feedback loop between the
4:105:7341:18:18:56:538:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exchange rate and banks’ net worth.  A decline in banks’ net worth depresses investment,
4:106:7429:18:18:56:538:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which  reduces  expected  future  wages  and  consumers’  demand  for  non-tradable  goods,
4:107:7520:18:18:56:538:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:causing  a  real  exchange  rate  depreciation.   An  exchange  rate  depreciation,  then,  reduces
4:108:7619:18:18:56:538:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:banks’  net  worth  if  they  have  foreign  currency  liabilities  and  domestic  currency  assets.
4:109:7719:18:18:56:538:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Thus, an economy with enough foreign currency debt is exposed to a crisis in which banks’
4:110:7808:18:21:56:495:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:net worth, the real exchange rate, and consumers’ income all fall at the same time.
4:111:7891:21:18:70:538:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The key aspect of our paper is to study how the comovement caused by financial crises
4:112:7976:18:18:56:538:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:influences the ex ante portfolio decisions of consumers and bankers regarding the currency
4:113:8066:18:18:56:538:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:denomination of their financial positions. When crises are possible in the future, consumers
4:114:8158:18:18:56:538:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have an incentive to insure by saving in foreign currency because of the hedging properties
4:115:8249:18:18:56:538:333:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:highlighted  above:  in  a  crisis,  consumers’  income  goes  down  while  the  foreign  currency
4:116:8347:18:18:56:538:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:appreciates.  In general equilibrium, this means that the interest rate in domestic currency
4:117:8439:18:18:56:538:297:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will be high relative to the interest rate in foreign currency, making foreign currency bor-
4:118:8531:18:18:56:538:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rowing relatively cheaper for banks. This mechanism can dominate the banks’ own motives
4:119:8618:18:21:56:401:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to insure against a crisis, leading them to issue more dollar debt.
4:120:8685:21:18:70:538:240:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This feedback between the insurance motives of consumers and the risk of future crises
4:121:8771:18:18:56:538:222:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can  be  so  strong  as  to  produce  multiple  equilibria.   In  asafeequilibrium,  consumers  are
4:122:8870:18:19:56:538:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not worried about future crises and are happy to save in domestic currency, banks borrow
4:123:8958:19:18:56:538:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mostly in domestic currency, the balance sheet effects of currency depreciation are weak,
4:124:9047:18:18:56:538:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and crises cannot occur.  This confirms consumers’ expectations.  In afragileequilibrium,
4:125:9136:18:18:56:538:149:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:consumers are worried about future crises and save in foreign currency. Domestic currency
4:126:9225:18:18:56:538:131:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:funding is more expensive, so banks borrow in dollars, making the financial sector more
4:127:9312:18:18:56:538:113:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fragile and opening the door to the possibility of a crisis.  Again, consumers’ expectations
4:128:9404:18:0:56:538:95:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are confirmed.  This novel form of multiplicity emphasizes the importance of allowing for
5:129:9494:0:21:56:479:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:endogenous risk premia as determinants of the currency denomination of debt.
5:130:9570:21:18:70:538:715:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The presence of these fragile equilibria motivates our analysis of lending of last resort.
5:131:9660:18:18:56:538:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We consider  the problem  of a  benevolent government  that can  extend a  liquidity facility
5:132:9753:18:18:56:538:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to the banks when a crisis takes place.  Although these interventions can break the feed-
5:133:9842:18:18:56:538:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:back loop between exchange rates and banks’ net worth, we show that a government with
5:134:9927:18:18:56:538:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:limited fiscal resources might be unable to credibly eliminate the crisis equilibrium.  The
5:135:10018:18:18:56:538:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reason is that when private investors hold pessimistic expectations, they also forecast low
5:136:10109:18:18:56:538:607:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:future tax revenues, and they are reluctant to purchase government debt.  This constrains
5:137:10198:18:19:56:538:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the government’s ability to finance the liquidity facilities and to lead the economy out of
5:138:10289:19:18:56:538:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the crisis.  In this context, we show that foreign currency reserves hedge the fiscal position
5:139:10383:18:18:56:538:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the government because they appreciate precisely when the private investors hold pes-
5:140:10471:18:18:56:538:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simistic expectations. When sufficiently large, the ex ante accumulation of foreign currency
5:141:10563:18:18:56:538:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reserves allows the government to credibly operate as a lender of last resort and eliminates
5:142:10655:18:21:56:172:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the crisis equilibrium.
5:143:10678:21:18:70:538:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This last set of results provides a rationale to the view, articulated by several economists
5:144:10770:18:18:56:538:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and policymakers, that emerging market authorities recently accumulated large quantities
5:145:10858:18:18:56:538:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of foreign currency reserves in order to improve financial stability.3In our framework, for-
5:146:10950:18:18:56:538:423:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:eign currency reserves help financial stability because they have good hedging properties
5:147:11039:18:18:56:538:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:against bad equilibria.  In other words, a desirable feature of foreign currency reserves is
5:148:11131:18:18:56:538:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that if private sector beliefs deteriorate, pushing the economy toward a crisis, the value of
5:149:11224:18:21:56:433:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reserves increases, giving the government more resources to intervene.
5:150:11294:21:18:70:538:348:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Importantly, the accumulation of official foreign currency reserves does not induce the
5:151:11381:18:18:56:538:330:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:banking sector to increase risk taking ex ante,  as the standard moral hazard logic would
5:152:11470:18:18:56:538:312:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:suggest.  When the government can credibly rule out financial panics, it also reduces the
5:153:11559:18:18:56:538:294:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:incentives  of  domestic  savers  to  hold  foreign  currency  assets  for  precautionary  reasons.
5:154:11658:18:18:56:538:276:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Through this mechanism, ex post interventions reduce the costs of borrowing in domestic
5:155:11745:18:18:56:538:258:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:currency, deterring banks from borrowing in foreign currency.  In this sense, official hold-
5:156:11837:18:18:56:538:240:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ings of foreign currency reserves can play a catalytic role by encouraging virtuous behavior
5:157:11929:18:40:56:525:222:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of local borrowers and by promoting financial stability also from an ex ante perspective.
5:158:12018:40:18:56:538:182:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Literature.Our  research  is  related  to  several  strands  of  literature.   Following  the  crises
5:159:12119:18:18:56:538:164:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the late 1990s,  several authors have developed equilibrium models to explain the joint
5:160:12209:18:19:56:538:146:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:occurrence of financial and currency crises.  The seminal work of Krugman (1999) empha-
5:161:12296:19:16:73:538:127:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:3For example, in a speech as governor of the Bank of England, Mervyn King argues that the buildup of
5:162:12396:16:12:56:538:111:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:foreign currency reserves allows emerging market authorities to act as “do-it-yourself lenders of last resort
5:163:12505:12:0:56:309:99:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:in US dollars to their own financial system” (King, 2006).
6:164:12564:0:18:56:538:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sizes how the feedback between investment demand and the real exchange rate can lead to
6:165:12651:18:18:56:538:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:multiple equilibria when firms/financial institutions have dollar debt.  Other seminal con-
6:166:12742:18:18:56:538:700:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tributions in this literature includeAghion, Bacchetta, and Banerjee(2001,2004),Burnside,
6:167:12831:18:18:56:538:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Eichenbaum, and Rebelo(2001b),Corsetti, Pesenti, and Roubini(1999),Chang and Velasco
6:168:12915:18:18:56:538:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2000,2001).  An important innovation relative to this literature is that we endogenize debt
6:169:13007:18:18:56:538:646:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:denomination and show how risk premia can lead banks to endogenously choose currency
6:170:13091:18:21:56:293:628:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:positions that expose an economy to a crisis.
6:171:13136:21:18:70:538:607:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The economic mechanism that produces foreign currency debt in our setting are distinct
6:172:13222:18:19:56:538:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from other explanations offered in the literature and, in particular, fromSchneider and Tor-
6:173:13314:19:18:56:538:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nell(2004),Burnside, Eichenbaum, and Rebelo(2001a) andFarhi and Tirole(2012).  These
6:174:13398:18:18:56:538:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:papers emphasize the role of bailout guarantees that, coupled with the financial instabil-
6:175:13488:18:18:56:538:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ity  typical  of  emerging  markets,  can  induce  the  private  sector  to  take  excessive  risk  and
6:176:13591:18:18:56:538:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:borrow in foreign currency.4In contrast, we emphasize the portfolio choices of domestic
6:177:13678:18:18:56:538:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:savers  and  how  their  demand  for  safety  can,  through  a  general  equilibrium  mechanism,
6:178:13774:18:18:56:538:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:incentivize local borrowers to issue dollar debt.  As explained earlier, our theory has dis-
6:179:13866:18:18:56:538:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tinctive predictions for the coexistence of asset and liability dollarization and for deviations
6:180:13962:18:18:56:538:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from uncovered interest parity that finds support in the data. Another key difference lies in
6:181:14055:18:18:56:538:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the effects of policy:  in the moral hazard view, ex post government interventions generate
6:182:14146:18:18:56:538:408:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:risk shifting and lead to more dollar debt; in our theory, these interventions can reduce the
6:183:14239:18:21:56:313:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:degree of financial dollarization in the economy.
6:184:14288:21:18:70:538:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our approach to lending of last resort is close toGertler and Kiyotaki(2015).  In their
6:185:14375:18:18:56:538:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:environment, providing liquidity to the financial sector during a panic has ex ante benefits,
6:186:14468:18:18:56:538:333:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  it  is  always  optimal  ex  post  because  the  government  does  not  face  borrowing  con-
6:187:14566:18:18:56:538:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:straints.  The main innovation in our paper relative to their approach is that we explicitly
6:188:14658:18:18:56:538:297:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:formulate a game between the government and private investors,  which embeds equilib-
6:189:14743:18:18:56:538:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rium in goods and asset markets.  This allows us to analyze whether off-the-equilibrium-
6:190:14831:18:18:56:538:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:path promises to intervene in a “bad” equilibrium are credible and to discuss how limited
6:191:14920:18:19:56:538:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fiscal  capacity  can  interfere  with  lending  of  last  resort  policies.   The  only  previous  work
6:192:15024:19:18:56:538:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we know of that discusses credibility issues in lending of last resort policies isEnnis and
6:193:15115:18:21:56:519:206:12:g_d0_f3:9:g_d0_f3:B:Keister(2009), who analyze deposit freezes in theDiamond and Dybvig(1983) model.5
6:194:15196:21:18:70:538:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A few papers address financial dollarization from a portfolio perspective.  In particular,
6:195:15286:18:19:56:538:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Ize  and  Levy-Yeyati(2003)  present  a  model  that  focuses  on  the  effects  of  the  monetary
6:196:15384:19:16:73:538:148:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:4On the normative side,Caballero and Krishnamurthy(2003) suggest that dollar debt might be excessive
6:197:15484:16:8:56:345:132:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:relative to the social optimum because of pecuniary externalities.
6:198:15550:8:16:73:538:124:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:5A  different  approach  to  think  about  the  fiscal  costs  of  intervention  is  to  consider  the  policy  maker’s
6:199:15669:16:0:56:524:108:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:uncertainty on whether a crisis is due to illiquidity or insolvency, an approach pursued inRobatto(2017).
7:200:15775:0:18:56:537:736:12:g_d0_f3:9:g_d0_f3:B:regime,  which  determines  the  volatility  of  inflation  and  of  the  nominal  exchange  rate.6
7:201:15874:18:18:56:538:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Salomao and Varela(2017) build a partial equilibrium model of the response of domestic
7:202:15960:18:18:56:538:700:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:borrowers to UIP violations and use it to generate cross-sectional predictions on the cur-
7:203:16050:18:18:56:538:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rency composition of debt.Gopinath and Stein(2018) present a model where the choice
7:204:16133:18:18:56:538:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  debt  denomination  comes  from  a  stylized  portfolio  problem  and  use  it  to  study  the
7:205:16231:18:18:56:538:646:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:complementarity between dollar invoicing and financial dollarization in the international
7:206:16320:18:19:56:538:628:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:monetary system.  A distinctive feature of our paper relative to this literature is the focus
7:207:16413:19:20:56:413:609:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the hedging benefits of dollar assets against financial instability.
7:208:16484:20:19:70:538:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:An important literature studies the role of foreign currency reserves as insurance against
7:209:16574:19:18:56:538:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:various  types  of  shocks  (Caballero  and  Panageas,2008;Durdu,  Mendoza,  and  Terrones,
7:210:16665:18:18:56:538:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2009;Jeanne  and  Rancière,2011;Bianchi,  Hatchondo,  and  Martinez,2012).   Relative  to
7:211:16754:18:18:56:538:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this  literature,  our  focus  on  reserves’  role  to  fight  financial  panics  leads  to  a  distinct  set
7:212:16863:18:18:56:538:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of predictions.7In particular, our model can rationalize why reserves across countries are
7:213:16953:18:18:56:538:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:well explained by the size of the financial sector’s total liabilities,  as shown byObstfeld,
7:214:17046:18:18:56:538:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Shambaugh, and Taylor(2010).  Moreover, our framework can explain why reserves seem
7:215:17129:18:18:56:538:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to be underutilized by domestic authorities, as documented byAizenman and Sun(2012).
7:216:17213:18:18:56:538:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In our framework, a government that accumulates enough reserves can rule out financial
7:217:17299:18:21:56:319:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:panics, so reserves are never used in equilibrium.
7:218:17349:21:18:70:538:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Finally,  our  paper  relates  to  recent  research  aimed  at  understanding  the  patterns  of
7:219:17445:18:18:56:538:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:global  capital  flows  and  low  interest  rates  in  the  world  economy  (Caballero,  Farhi,  and
7:220:17545:18:18:56:538:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Gourinchas,2008;Gourinchas and Jeanne,2013;Mendoza, Quadrini, and Rios-Rull,2009;
7:221:17626:18:18:56:538:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Maggiori,2017;Fahri and Maggiori,2017). Our paper offers a fully fledged model of finan-
7:222:17714:18:18:56:538:333:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cial instability as a cause for increased accumulation of reserves by emerging economies,
7:223:17803:18:18:56:538:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and it identifies important differences between the private and the official sector demand
7:224:17893:18:39:56:114:297:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for dollars.
7:225:17905:39:18:56:538:258:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Layout.Section2 presents the model.  We then move on to characterize the equilibria of
7:226:17991:18:19:56:538:240:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the model, proceeding backward in time. Section3 describes the continuation equilibria of
7:227:18080:19:18:56:538:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the model from period 1 onward, taking the currency denomination of assets and liabilities
7:228:18170:18:18:56:538:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as given.  Section4 studies the optimal portfolio choices of households and banks in the
7:229:18258:18:18:56:538:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:initial  period.   In  Section5  we  introduce  a  government  and  study  lending  of  last  resort,
7:230:18359:18:19:56:500:167:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:while Section6 discusses the role of foreign currency reserves. Section7 concludes.
7:231:18442:19:16:73:538:148:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:6Rappoport (2009) adds defaultable debt and optimal monetary policy to the setup ofIze and Levy-Yeyati
7:232:18544:16:9:56:536:132:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:(2003) and obtains the possibility of multiple equilibria due to the endogenous response of monetary policy.
7:233:18652:9:15:73:539:123:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:7Models that focus on other sources of equilibrium multiplicity areHur and Kondo(2016) andHernandez
7:234:18751:15:0:56:85:108:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:(2017).
8:235:18759:0:33:56:133:735:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:2    Model
8:236:18769:33:19:56:538:702:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We consider a small open economy that lasts three periods,t=0, 1, 2, populated by two
8:237:18854:19:18:56:538:683:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:groups  of  domestic  agents,  consumers  and  bankers,  who  trade  with  a  large  number  of
8:238:18949:18:18:56:538:665:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:foreign investors. There are two goods in the economy, a tradable good and a non-tradable
8:239:19038:18:21:56:86:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:good.
8:240:19043:21:18:70:538:626:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The model is built around three ingredients.  First, in line with standard financial accel-
8:241:19134:18:18:56:538:608:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:erator models, bankers have unique access to a superior technology to accumulate capital,
8:242:19223:18:18:56:538:590:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and they finance capital accumulation with debt. Second, debt can be denominated in non-
8:243:19311:18:18:56:538:572:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tradable or tradable goods, which is meant to capture debt denominated in domestic and
8:244:19397:18:18:56:538:554:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:foreign currency. This creates the possibility of currency mismatch. Third, consumers sup-
8:245:19487:18:18:56:538:536:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ply labor that is combined with capital to produce tradable output.  This last assumption
8:246:19576:18:18:56:538:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:introduces a simple macro spillover by which consumers’ incomes go down when bankers’
8:247:19661:18:21:56:271:500:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:capacity to accumulate capital contracts.
8:248:19702:21:18:70:538:479:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We now turn to a detailed description of the environment. The model includes a number
8:249:19787:18:43:56:509:461:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of simplifying assumptions. Their role is discussed in detail at the end of the section.
8:250:19875:43:30:56:324:418:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.1    Agents and their decision problems
8:251:19916:30:33:56:471:388:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Consumers.Consumers have preferences represented by the utility function
8:252:19988:33:12:263:287:355:12:g_d0_f6:17:g_d0_f7:C:E∑
8:253:19990:12:0:279:282:343:9:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f4:F:t
8:254:19991:0:42:290:331:355:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f5:C:βtU(ct)
8:255:19998:42:33:56:490:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereU(ct) =c1−γt/(1−γ)andctis the Cobb-Douglas consumption aggregator
8:256:20068:33:33:247:348:280:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:ct= (cTt)ω(cNt)1−ω,
8:257:20087:33:21:56:533:247:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:B:cTtis consumption of the tradable good, andcNtis consumption of the non-tradable good.
8:258:20173:21:18:70:538:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The tradable good is the numeraire, andptdenotes the price of the non-tradable good.
8:259:20257:18:18:56:538:208:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Each periodt, consumers supply a unit of labor inelastically at the wagewtand receive an
8:260:20345:18:21:56:262:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:endowment of non-tradable goodseNc,t.
8:261:20382:21:18:70:538:169:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Consumers  trade  one-period  bonds  denominated  in  tradable  and  non-tradable  goods,
8:262:20471:18:18:56:538:151:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:denoted  byaTtandaNt,  at  the  pricesqTtandqNt.    As  just  mentioned,  these  two  bonds
8:263:20562:18:18:56:538:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:represent foreign and domestic currency denominated bonds. Currency denomination can
8:264:20646:18:18:56:538:115:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be modeled in other ways—for example, by denominating domestic bonds in terms of the
8:265:20730:18:0:56:538:97:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:domestic consumption basket, or by introducing explicitly nominal variables and making
9:266:20817:0:18:56:538:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assumptions about monetary policy.  For our purposes here, simply denominating bonds
9:267:20901:18:21:56:421:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in tradables and non-tradables makes the analysis more transparent.
9:268:20968:21:33:70:263:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The consumers’ budget constraint is
9:269:21003:33:33:148:538:664:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:cTt+ptcNt+qTtaTt+1+qNtptaNt+1≤wt+pteNc,t+aTt+ptaNt.(1)
9:270:21057:33:18:56:538:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Consumers choose consumption levels and asset positions in order to maximize their utility
9:271:21147:18:39:56:460:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:subject to the budget constraint (1) and the terminal conditionaN3=aT3=0.
9:272:21220:39:18:56:538:574:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Bankers.Bankers  are  risk-neutral  agents  and  consume  only  tradable  goods  at  date  2.
9:273:21313:18:18:56:538:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Bankers own banks. Banks hold physical capitalkt, which is used as input in the production
9:274:21403:18:19:56:538:538:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  tradable  goods  and  yields  the  rental  ratert.  Banks  have  access  to  a  linear  technology
9:275:21505:19:18:56:538:519:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to convert one unit of tradable goods into one unit of capital and vice versa.  Capital fully
9:276:21598:18:18:56:538:501:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:depreciates at the end of each period.  Banks also receive a non-tradable endowment each
9:277:21686:18:18:56:538:483:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:periodeNb,t. On the liability side, banks issue tradable and non-tradable denominated bonds,
9:278:21778:18:18:56:538:465:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:denoted, respectively, bybTtandbNt.  The banks’ net worth at the beginning of each period
9:279:21867:18:18:56:65:447:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is
9:280:21869:18:26:220:538:429:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:nt=rtkt+pteNb,t−bTt−ptbNt.(2)
9:281:21898:26:33:56:278:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The banks’ budget constraint att=0, 1 is

9:286:22187:18:18:56:538:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:liabilities to be bounded, in each state of the world, by a fraction of the capital held by the
9:287:22282:18:18:56:85:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bank:
9:288:22287:18:26:234:538:244:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:bTt+1+pt+1bNt+1≤θkt+1,(4)

9:293:22648:18:18:56:538:143:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of motion for net worth (2), the budget constraint (3), the collateral constraint (4), and the

10:303:22870:0:18:56:539:736:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Production.Consumers own two types of firms.  Tradable goods firms produce tradable
10:304:22953:18:33:56:414:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:goods using capital and labor according to the production function
10:305:23019:33:33:262:538:685:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:yTt=KαtL1−αt,(5)

10:307:23076:21:18:70:538:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Next,  there  are  firms  that  produce  capital ̃ktusing  a  linear  technology  that  requires
10:308:23172:18:18:56:539:613:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:B:φ>1 units of tradable goods per unit of capital.  Since the latter technology is inferior to
10:309:23264:18:18:56:538:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the banks’ technology, these firms will only be active when banks’ capital is low enough,
10:310:23353:18:21:56:172:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as we will see shortly.
10:311:23376:21:18:70:538:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Both types of firms owned by consumers run constant returns to scale technologies, so
10:312:23461:18:18:56:538:538:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their profits will be zero in equilibrium and can be omitted from the consumers’ budget
10:313:23548:18:21:56:117:520:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:constraints.
10:314:23560:21:33:70:506:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We assume that the total endowment of non-tradable goods is constant over time:
10:315:23639:33:39:259:336:466:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:eNc,t+eNb,t=eN.
10:316:23654:39:19:56:538:427:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f3:B:Foreign investors.Foreign investors are risk neutral and consume only tradable goods.
10:317:23739:19:18:56:538:408:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Their discount factor isβ.  An important restriction in our model is that foreign investors
10:318:23830:18:43:56:413:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can only purchase tradable denominated bonds, denoted by{aT∗t}.
10:319:23893:43:29:56:170:347:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.2    Equilibrium
10:320:23911:29:19:56:538:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:There  are  no  fundamental  shocks  in  the  economy,  but  given  the  possibility  of  multiple
10:321:24009:19:18:56:538:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibria, we introduce a sunspot variableζrealized att=1, with a uniform distribution
10:322:24096:18:18:56:538:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on[0, 1], and use this sunspot as a selection device when multiple equilibria are possible at
10:323:24189:18:18:56:538:263:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:B:t=1. For ease of notation, we will mostly leave implicit the dependence of variables dated
10:324:24279:18:30:56:243:245:12:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f3:C:t=1, 2 on the sunspot realization.9
10:325:24314:30:18:56:538:215:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:C:Definition 1.A competitive equilibrium is a vector of prices{pt,rt,wt,qTt,qNt}, households’ choices
10:326:24413:18:18:56:539:197:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f4:C:{cTt,cNt,aTt+1,aNt+1}, bankers’ choices{kt+1,bTt+1,bNt+1}, firms’ choices{Kt,Lt, ̃kt}, and foreign in-
10:327:24515:18:33:56:490:179:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:vestors’ choices{aT∗t}such that all choices are individually optimal and all markets clear,
10:328:24606:33:16:159:436:146:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:cNt=eN,aTt+aT∗t=bTt,aNt=bNt,Kt=kt+ ̃kt.
10:329:24645:16:15:73:538:130:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:9We only introduce a sunspot att=1 because,  conditional on past state variables,  no multiplicity can
10:330:24747:15:12:56:538:115:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:arise att=2, and we do not need to specify how multiplicity is resolved att=0, given that no previous
10:331:24848:12:0:56:252:103:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:decision relies on that equilibrium selection.
11:332:24895:0:18:70:538:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For simplicity, throughout the paper we focus on economies in which at datet=0, in
11:333:24977:18:44:56:531:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium, there is no investment in the inferior technology, that is,K1=k1and ̃k1=0.
11:334:25064:44:29:56:266:674:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.3    Discussion of assumptions
11:335:25096:29:21:56:442:645:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Let us briefly discuss some simplifying assumptions made in the model.
11:336:25166:21:18:70:538:624:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:First, banks invest directly in physical capital, rather than making loans.  This is a fairly
11:337:25259:18:18:56:538:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:common assumption in the financial accelerator literature,  and it essentially consolidates
11:338:25350:18:18:56:538:588:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:into a unique entity the banks and the firms they lend to. In terms of capturing the problem
11:339:25442:18:18:56:538:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of liability dollarization, this assumption treats in the same way situations in which banks’
11:340:25535:18:18:56:538:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:balance sheets are explicitly mismatched and situations in which they are only implicitly
11:341:25624:18:18:56:538:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mismatched—as happens, for example, when banks borrow in dollars and lend in dollars
11:342:25708:18:21:56:507:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to domestic firms, who are then more likely to default in the event of a depreciation.
11:343:25794:21:18:70:538:495:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Second,  foreign  investors  in  the  model  can  only  hold  tradable  bonds,  an  assumption
11:344:25888:18:18:56:538:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that plays an important role in our analysis, as we will discuss in Section 4.4.  Our results,
11:345:25982:18:18:56:538:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:however, do not require this stark form of segmentation, and they would go through as long
11:346:26072:18:19:56:538:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as the demand for domestic currency (non-tradable) claims by foreigners is not infinitely
11:347:26161:19:18:56:538:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:elastic.  Ruling out foreign investors’ participation in the domestic currency debt market is
11:348:26254:18:21:56:200:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:just a useful simplification.
11:349:26283:21:18:70:538:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Third, we are assuming that non-tradables are in fixed endowment.  This simplifies the
11:350:26369:18:18:56:538:365:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:analysis because we do not have to determine how labor is allocated among the two sectors
11:351:26458:18:18:56:538:347:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and only need to keep track of capital accumulation in one sector.  Our main results can
11:352:26546:18:18:56:538:329:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:also be derived in a more symmetric version of the model with production in both sectors,
11:353:26635:18:43:56:242:311:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:but the analysis is less transparent.
11:354:26672:43:30:56:155:268:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.4    Road map
11:355:26687:30:18:56:538:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In  the  next  two  sections,  we  analyze  the  model  in  two  steps,  moving  backward  in  time.
11:356:26787:18:18:56:538:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:First,  we  analyze  the  equilibrium  in  the  last  two  periods,  taking  as  given  assets  and  lia-
11:357:26892:18:18:56:538:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bilities from the previous period.  We call this acontinuation equilibriumand show that, for
11:358:26984:18:18:56:538:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:some initial conditions, multiple continuation equilibria are possible.  In our second step,
11:359:27076:18:18:56:538:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we go back to date 0 and complete our equilibrium characterization, focusing, in particular,
11:360:27168:18:18:56:538:148:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the endogenous denomination of assets and liabilities and on whether the economy can
11:361:27255:18:0:56:482:130:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:endogenously settle on portfolios that produce multiple continuation equilibria.
12:362:27336:0:33:56:204:735:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:3    Financial crises
12:363:27357:33:19:56:538:702:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In  this  section,  we  look  at  continuation  equilibria,  that  is,  equilibria  that  arise  at  dates
12:364:27463:19:18:56:538:683:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:B:t=1, 2, for given initial asset positions{aT1,aN1,bT1,bN1,K1}.  We characterize continuation
12:365:27555:18:18:56:538:665:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibria  using  two  relations.   The  first  is  an  equilibrium  condition  in  the  non-tradable
12:366:27657:18:43:56:462:647:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:goods market. The second is an equilibrium condition in the capital market.

13:398:29249:0:29:56:186:736:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.2    Capital market

13:407:29677:18:21:56:146:565:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:B:n1≥(1−βθ)K∗.

13:409:29791:18:18:56:538:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investment in the inferior capital accumulation technology controlled by the consumers. In
13:410:29881:18:35:56:462:508:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this case, the level ofK2can be derived from the bankers’ budget constraint:

16:493:34524:33:18:70:538:703:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The improvement in the current account shows that the domestic banking crisis is asso-

16:495:34706:18:18:56:538:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ment is driven by the reduction in banks’ net worth, while the contraction in consumption

16:502:35266:18:18:56:538:538:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lower  because  of  lower  capital  accumulation  and  hence  lower  future  real  wages.  On  the

16:505:35548:18:43:56:415:483:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:gives a sufficient condition under which the latter effect dominates.

17:546:37795:21:18:70:538:257:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Since  mismatch  is  crucial  for  the  presence  of  multiplicity,  our  next  question  is:   why
17:547:37894:18:18:56:538:239:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:would  banks  choose  a  liability  composition  at  date  0  that  exposes  them  to  crises  with
17:548:37993:18:50:56:489:221:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:positive probability at date 1? This is the question we address in the next section.
17:549:38077:50:34:56:187:171:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:4    Dollarization
17:550:38095:34:18:56:538:137:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We  now  go  back  to  date  0  and  study  the  equilibrium  determination  of  banks’  and  con-
17:551:38193:18:18:56:538:119:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sumers’ assets and liabilities.  Our main objective is to show that even though banks can
17:552:38282:18:0:56:538:101:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:choose ex ante whether to denominate their debt in tradables or non-tradables, this does not
18:553:38376:0:18:56:538:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rule out the possibility of multiple continuation equilibria.  That is, even though currency
18:554:38468:18:18:56:538:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mismatch in banks’ balance sheets opens the door to “bad” Pareto-dominated equilibria,
18:555:38554:18:18:56:538:700:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:banks  do  not  necessarily  have  sufficient  ex  ante  incentives  to  reduce  their  exchange  rate
18:556:38656:18:21:56:107:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exposure.
18:557:38665:21:18:70:538:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:From now on, whenever we say an “equilibrium” of the model, we are referring to an
18:558:38747:18:18:56:538:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium of the whole three-period model, as opposed to a continuation equilibrium that
18:559:38837:18:18:56:538:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:starts in period 1.  We will use the following terminology.  We say that an equilibrium is
18:560:38927:18:18:56:538:607:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:“fragile” if it features multiple continuation equilibria that happen with positive probability
18:561:39022:18:19:56:538:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f9:B:att=1. We say that an equilibrium is “safe” if the equilibrium values of{aT1,aN1,bT1,bN1,K1}
18:562:39114:19:18:56:538:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are  such  that  there  is  a  unique  continuation  equilibrium.   Notice  that  the  requirement
18:563:39212:18:18:56:538:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for  a  safe  equilibrium  is  not  just  that  a  single  continuation  equilibrium  is  selected  with
18:564:39316:18:21:56:462:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:probability 1 att=1, but also that no other continuation equilibrium exists.
18:565:39392:21:18:70:538:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our argument in this section is constructive.  First, we show how to construct examples
18:566:39479:18:18:56:538:495:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of fragile equilibria.  Second, we show that given an economy with a fragile equilibrium,
18:567:39568:18:18:56:538:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the same economy also admits a safe equilibrium and we compare the two equilibria.  At
18:568:39654:18:18:56:538:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the end of this section, we use a numerical example to illustrate our argument and provide
18:569:39744:18:43:56:511:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intuition. Readers less interested in the formal steps can skip directly to the example.
18:570:39832:43:30:56:192:398:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.1    Portfolio choice
18:571:39855:30:18:56:538:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Consider first the portfolio decision problem of consumers and banks at date 0. Consumers’
18:572:39945:18:37:56:424:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:optimization gives the following first-order conditions foraT1andaN1:
18:573:40014:37:0:177:365:313:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:C:qT0λc,0=βE[λc,1],qN0λc,0=βE
18:574:40041:0:9:367:373:330:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:[

18:577:40046:0:0:388:406:313:12:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f3:C:λc,1

18:579:40051:17:36:415:538:313:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:,(14)
18:580:40056:36:18:56:89:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where
18:581:40061:18:26:247:347:259:12:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f3:C:λc,t= (cTt)ω(1−γ)−1
18:582:40080:26:21:56:365:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is the consumers’ marginal utility of wealth (in tradables).
18:583:40140:21:18:70:538:212:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:On the banks’ side, we will focus on cases in which the collateral constraint is slack at
18:584:40229:18:38:56:481:194:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time 0. The banks’ first-order conditions forbT1andbN1then take a similar form:
18:585:40308:38:0:183:358:156:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f6:C:qT0λb,0=E[λb,1],qN0λb,0=E
18:586:40333:0:8:360:366:173:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:[
18:587:40334:8:17:369:379:165:12:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f3:C:p1
18:588:40336:17:0:369:379:148:12:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f3:C:p0
18:589:40338:0:0:381:400:156:12:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f3:C:λb,1
18:590:40342:0:17:400:406:173:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:]
18:591:40343:17:0:409:412:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:,
19:592:40346:0:36:56:340:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the bankers’ marginal utility of wealth att=1 is
19:593:40398:36:0:260:292:700:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f5:C:λb,1=
19:594:40403:0:16:298:328:708:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:C:r2−θ
19:595:40407:16:0:297:330:692:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f8:A:1−βθ
19:596:40411:0:36:332:335:700:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:.
19:597:40412:36:18:56:538:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:To interpret the last expression notice that a unit of net worth can be levered to purchase
19:598:40503:18:18:56:538:646:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1/(1−βθ)units of capital att=1.  And the payoff per unit of capital att=2, net of debt
19:599:40589:18:21:56:509:628:12:g_d0_f3:9:g_d0_f3:B:repayments, isr2−θ. So we get a return of(r2−θ)/(1−βθ)per unit of net worth.13
19:600:40667:21:18:70:538:607:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:It is useful to remark that when multiple equilibria are possible, the bankers’ marginal
19:601:40755:18:18:56:538:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:utility of wealth is higher in the bad equilibrium, since in that equilibrium capital is scarcer
19:602:40851:18:18:56:538:571:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and yields a higher rate of return. Therefore, even though bankers are risk neutral, they still
19:603:40946:18:18:56:538:553:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:perceive a high marginal utility of wealth in states of the world in which their net worth
19:604:41036:18:18:56:538:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is low.  This is a hedging motive that commonly arises in general equilibrium models with
19:605:41125:18:44:56:516:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial constraints, as pointed out, for example, in Rampini and Viswanathan (2010).
19:606:41211:44:29:56:218:473:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.2    Fragile equilibrium
19:607:41237:29:18:56:538:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Take a vector of date 1 initial positions{aT1,aN1,bT1,bN1,K1}such that multiple continuation
19:608:41329:18:18:56:538:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibria are possible.  Suppose now that we want to construct an equilibrium in which
19:609:41416:18:19:56:538:408:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the two stable continuation equilibria occur with positive probability.  Given that the price
19:610:41509:19:18:57:538:389:12:g_d0_f4:9:g_d0_f3:C:p1is different in the two equilibria and there are only two states of the world att=1,14
19:611:41597:18:18:56:538:371:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:domestic consumers and bankers have sufficient instruments to achieve perfect risk sharing
19:612:41687:18:18:56:538:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:among themselves. This means that the portfolio conditions derived above can be satisfied
19:613:41776:18:18:56:538:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:if and only if the marginal utilities of wealth of consumers and bankers are equalized across
19:614:41869:18:18:56:538:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:states of the world, using the appropriate Pareto weights.  That is, the portfolio conditions
19:615:41962:18:36:56:350:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can be satisfied if and only if there is aΦ>0 such that
19:616:42017:36:0:229:329:263:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f8:C:(cT1)ω(1−γ)−1=Φβ
19:617:42033:0:16:332:362:271:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:C:r2−θ
19:618:42037:16:28:330:363:255:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f8:A:1−βθ
19:619:42041:28:21:56:316:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in both the good and the continuation equilibria.
19:620:42090:21:18:70:538:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Can we construct an equilibrium in which the last condition is satisfied?  The answer is
19:621:42178:18:18:56:538:188:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:yes because both the consumers’ and the bankers’ marginal utilities of wealth are higher if
19:622:42269:18:18:56:538:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the bad equilibrium is realized. Building on this intuition, the next proposition shows how
19:623:42360:18:19:56:525:152:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to construct a fragile equilibrium and what conditions are required for the construction.
19:624:42449:19:16:69:538:133:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:13The expression is also valid ifr2=1/βand banks are unconstrained.  Then the expression boils down
19:625:42548:16:9:56:410:117:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:toλb,t=1/β, as the return per unit of net worth is simply the interest rate 1/β.
19:626:42628:9:15:69:538:108:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:14To be precise, there are only two payoff-relevant states.  The sunspot is a continuous variable, but it can
19:627:42737:15:0:56:305:93:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:only select one of the two stable continuation equilibria.
20:628:42797:0:18:70:538:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For  simplicity,  we  focus  on  constructing  fragile  equilibria  in  which  non-tradable  posi-
20:629:42895:18:18:56:538:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions are exactly zero and in which, as mentioned above, the collateral constraint is slack

20:632:43100:30:18:56:538:652:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:C:Proposition 3.Fix all the model parameters exceptγand the initial asset positions at t=0.  Take

20:651:43986:18:21:56:228:342:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the proposition in the appendix.
20:652:44018:21:18:70:538:321:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Proposition  3relies  on  making  the  consumers  sufficiently  risk  averse  to  match  the
20:653:44110:18:18:56:538:303:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bankers’  hedging  motive.   This  logic  can  also  be  turned  around,  and  we  can  show  that
20:654:44208:18:18:56:538:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:if consumers’ risk aversion is low enough, then the economy cannot feature a fragile equi-
20:655:44298:18:30:56:465:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:librium. The next proposition provides a uniqueness result along these lines.
20:656:44375:30:37:56:341:237:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:C:Proposition 4.Suppose consumers’ risk aversion satisfies
20:657:44431:37:0:220:262:200:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f5:C:γ<1+

21:662:44510:0:29:56:201:736:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.3    Safe equilibrium
21:663:44533:29:19:56:538:707:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Suppose  we  have  constructed  an  example  of  an  economy  that  has  a  fragile  equilibrium
21:664:44629:19:18:56:538:688:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:following  the  steps  in  Proposition3.   We  can  then  ask  whether  the  same  economy  also
21:665:44725:18:30:56:469:670:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:admits a safe equilibrium. The next proposition shows that the answer is yes.
21:666:44802:30:18:56:538:640:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:C:Proposition 5.Take an economy with a fragile equilibrium constructed as in Proposition3.  The
21:667:44895:18:18:56:538:622:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:economy also has a safe equilibrium.  Comparing the safe and the fragile equilibria,  c0and  p0are
21:668:44993:18:33:56:349:604:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:higher and the trade balance is lower in the safe equilibrium.
21:669:45055:33:18:70:538:571:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  idea  behind  this  proposition  is  to  take  the  good  continuation  equilibrium  that  is
21:670:45153:18:18:56:538:553:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:part of the fragile equilibrium under consideration and rearrange the debt composition of
21:671:45242:18:18:56:538:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the bankers in favor of non-tradable debt in order to reduce the currency mismatch in their
21:672:45333:18:18:56:538:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:balance sheet. The logic of Figure2 suggests that this eventually eliminates the multiplicity
21:673:45426:18:18:56:538:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:while  leaving  total  repayments  in  the  good  equilibrium  unchanged.   Because  of  market
21:674:45521:18:18:56:538:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:clearing, this requires an increase in the consumers positions in non-tradable denominated
21:675:45611:18:18:56:538:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bonds, as market clearing requiresbN1=aN1.  This can always be done because consumers
21:676:45696:18:18:56:538:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are no longer worried about denominating their saving in non-tradables once the bad equi-
21:677:45785:18:21:56:499:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:librium is eliminated, as the depreciation risk associated with the crisis disappears.
21:678:45871:21:18:70:538:406:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The proposition states that the safe equilibrium has higher consumption and a more ap-
21:679:45957:18:18:56:538:388:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:preciated real exchange rate than the fragile equilibrium. This happens because consumers
21:680:46046:18:18:56:538:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:att=0  are  no  longer  concerned  about  the  bad  equilibrium  outcome,  and  this  reduces
21:681:46139:18:18:56:538:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their  incentives  to  save.   As  they  choose  higher  consumption  att=0,  their  demand  for
21:682:46235:18:18:56:539:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:non-tradables increase, and this pushes up the real exchange rate. The timet=0 choice of
21:683:46323:18:18:56:538:316:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:capital is, however, the same in the two equilibria. Because of full depreciation and inelastic
21:684:46418:18:18:56:538:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:labor,  the  marginal  product  of  capital  at  datet=1  is  state  uncontingent,  which  implies
21:685:46516:18:18:56:538:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that its rate of return is equalized to the rate of return on a bond denominated in tradable
21:686:46608:18:19:56:538:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:goods.  This result follows from the fact that the rate of return equals 1/βin both the safe
21:687:46700:19:43:56:191:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the fragile equilibria.

22:723:47657:37:18:56:538:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereλc,1is  the  consumers’  marginal  utility  of  wealth.   The  left-hand  side  of  equation

22:725:47845:18:21:56:389:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:compares the returns of bonds denominated in different units.
22:726:47906:21:18:70:538:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the safe equilibrium, consumers decide to denominate most of their savings in non-
22:727:47991:18:18:56:538:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tradables.  Banks absorb the desired pesos savings of consumers and issue tradable bonds
22:728:48079:18:18:56:538:316:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to finance any further shortfall between desired investment and their initial net worth. Be-
22:729:48171:18:18:56:538:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cause most of the banks’ liabilities are denominated in non-tradables, the banks have little
22:730:48263:18:18:56:538:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:currency mismatch on their balance sheets. Indeed, in our example there is no mismatch at
22:731:48352:18:18:56:538:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:all(bN1=eNb,1), and the economy has only a unique stable continuation equilibrium at date
22:732:48441:18:18:56:538:244:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:B:t=1.  This can be appreciated from the fact that consumers’ wages and the real exchange
22:733:48528:18:21:56:175:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate are not stochastic.
22:734:48552:21:18:70:538:205:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Why are theset=0 asset choices optimal from the perspective of consumers and banks?
22:735:48635:18:18:56:538:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The impossibility of the bad equilibrium at datet=1 means that agents in the economy
22:736:48719:18:18:56:538:169:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:do  not  face  any  risk.   Thus,  the  two  bonds  are  perfect  substitutes  as  their  interest  rate
22:737:48823:18:18:56:538:151:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is  equalized.   In  equilibrium,  this  is  precisely  what  happens  because  of  equation  (16).   It
22:738:48927:18:19:56:538:133:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:follows that in the safe equilibrium,  both consumers and banks are indifferent about the
22:739:49016:19:19:56:472:114:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:denomination of their assets and liabilities, which rationalizes these positions.
22:740:49097:19:0:69:496:95:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:15This condition can be derived by following standard steps from the optimality conditions (14).
23:741:49195:0:18:70:538:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In  the  fragile  equilibrium,  consumers  decide  to  denominate  their  savings  in  tradable
23:742:49290:18:18:56:538:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:goods(a∗1=0.17,aN1=0.00).  Banks have little access to pesos, and they finance their date
23:743:49379:18:18:56:538:700:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:B:t=0  operations  by  issuing  debt  denominated  in  tradable  goods.   This  balance  sheet  of
23:744:49475:18:18:56:538:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the banks generates currency mismatch(eNb,1>bN1), and it exposes the economy to a bad
23:745:49560:18:21:56:192:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium at datet=1.
23:746:49583:21:18:70:538:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  risk  of  a  bad  equilibrium  at  datet=1  is  what  justifies  the  portfolio  choices  of
23:747:49680:18:18:56:538:625:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:agents in the economy at datet=0.  From Table1, we can verify that consumers’ lifetime
23:748:49766:18:18:56:538:607:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:income  is  exposed  to  the  realization  of  the  sunspot  at  datet=1.   Importantly,  the  real
23:749:49865:18:19:56:538:589:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exchange rate depreciates when a crisis occurs, generating a negative comovement between
23:750:49953:19:18:56:538:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:consumers’ income and the real exchange rate.  This property of the exchange rate makes
23:751:50040:18:18:56:538:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bonds  denominated  in  tradable  goods  a  “crisis  hedge”  for  consumers,  and  this  justifies
23:752:50138:18:18:56:538:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their decision to denominate their savings in tradables att=0.  The precautionary motive
23:753:50226:18:18:56:538:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the households is met, in equilibrium, by a riskier balance sheet of the banks, which is
23:754:50317:18:21:56:378:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ultimately what exposes the economy to financial instability.
23:755:50378:21:18:70:538:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Why are banks happy to borrow in tradables and be exposed to exchange rate risk? The
23:756:50462:18:18:56:538:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:answer  is  that  borrowing  in  tradables  is  “cheaper”  for  banks.   This  can  be  seen  by  com-
23:757:50564:18:18:56:538:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:paring  the  interest  rates  of  the  two  bonds.   From  Table1,  we  can  see  that  in  the  fragile
23:758:50668:18:18:56:538:423:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium,  the rate of return on bonds denominated in tradables is lower than the one
23:759:50756:18:18:56:538:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on non-tradables.  This deviation from the UIP condition is effectively a result of the con-
23:760:50848:18:18:56:538:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sumers’ unwillingness to save in non-tradables, which in equilibrium bids up the interest
23:761:50937:18:18:56:538:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate  on  these  bonds.   Paradoxically,  this  behavior  generates  in  equilibrium  the  very  risk
23:762:51038:18:21:56:320:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:against which the consumers are trying to insure.
23:763:51087:21:18:70:538:330:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Before continuing, it is useful to further discuss properties of safe and fragile equilibria.
23:764:51180:18:18:56:538:312:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:As for the safe equilibrium,  we have seen that consumers and banks are indifferent over
23:765:51268:18:18:56:539:294:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their asset positions att=0.  Because of that, the split between tradable and non-tradable
23:766:51358:18:18:56:538:276:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bonds on the balance sheets of domestic agents is indeterminate, and there is a continuum
23:767:51447:18:18:56:538:258:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of safe equilibria. This is due to the absence of fundamental shocks, which implies that the
23:768:51539:18:21:56:231:240:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:safe equilibrium is deterministic.
23:769:51573:21:18:70:538:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As for the fragile equilibrium, it is worth emphasizing that a key assumption underlying
23:770:51661:18:18:56:538:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:its  existence  is  the  presence  of  segmentation  in  financial  markets.  The  segmentation  has
23:771:51761:18:21:56:315:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:both an international and a domestic dimension.
23:772:51808:21:18:70:538:162:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:At the international level, it is important that some mechanism prevents foreign investors
23:773:51898:18:18:56:538:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from  issuing  non-tradable  denominated  bonds  to  the  local  banks.   To  understand  why,
23:774:51992:18:19:56:538:126:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:consider the fragile equilibrium in Table1 and suppose that we allow foreign investors to
23:775:52081:19:18:56:538:107:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:purchase claims denominated in non-tradables.  Because foreign investors are risk neutral,
23:776:52171:18:0:56:538:89:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:they have an incentive at datet=0 to purchase those claims:  due to the UIP deviation,
24:777:52259:0:18:56:538:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:they earn a positive excess return from this strategy. Eventually, this force would eliminate
24:778:52352:18:18:56:538:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the fragile equilibrium because, by issuing non-tradable denominated claims, the balance
24:779:52440:18:18:56:538:700:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sheets of local banks become less exposed to exchange rate fluctuations.  Importantly, this
24:780:52531:18:18:56:538:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:argument works only because foreign investors are risk neutral and have deep pockets—
24:781:52616:18:18:56:538:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assumptions that generate an infinitely elastic supply of funds.  There is ample empirical
24:782:52706:18:18:56:538:646:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:evidence, however, that the supply of foreign capital to emerging market economies is not
24:783:52795:18:19:56:538:628:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:perfectly  elastic.16In  our  paper,  we  consider  the  extreme  view  in  which  the  supply  of
24:784:52893:19:18:56:538:609:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:foreign  funds  in  “local  currency”  (non-tradables)  is  perfectly  inelastic,  but  this  is  just  a
24:785:52998:18:18:56:538:591:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:useful simplification.  Our results would not be qualitatively different if we were to relax
24:786:53090:18:18:56:538:573:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this  assumption  and  instead  model  foreign  lenders  as  risk-averse  specialists  that  are  not
24:787:53191:18:21:56:289:555:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:diversified toward the small open economy.
24:788:53233:21:18:70:538:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:At the domestic level, we have assumed that the bankers and the consumers are distinct
24:789:53319:18:18:56:538:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:agents.   This  assumption,  shared  by  recent  papers  such  asBrunnermeier  and  Sannikov

24:792:53585:18:18:56:538:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:4, is important in obtaining the fragile equilibrium.  More primitive frictions that limit the
24:793:53679:18:49:56:537:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:participation of consumers to asset markets would offer a justification for our assumption.
24:794:53770:49:34:56:252:395:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:5    Lending of last resort

25:832:56448:18:33:56:511:275:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:government is benevolent, and its objective is to maximize the social welfare function
