29:983:63202:18:18:56:538:312:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:repeating the steps above, an additional dollar transfer to the banks changes social welfare
29:984:63294:18:21:56:69:294:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by
29:985:63296:21:0:156:255:273:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f8:C:−UcT(cT,eN) +Φβ
29:986:63311:0:16:259:288:281:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f8:C:r2−θ
29:987:63315:16:0:257:290:265:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f8:A:1−βθ
29:988:63319:0:0:294:313:273:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f8:C:+β
29:989:63321:0:13:316:323:286:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:(
29:990:63322:13:0:323:406:273:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f7:C:UcT(cT,eN)−Φ
29:991:63334:0:13:406:413:286:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:C:)
29:992:63335:13:30:416:439:273:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:dw2,
29:993:63339:30:18:56:538:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wheredw2=β(1−α)r2/(1−βθ)>0.  The first two terms are the same as before.  The
29:994:63416:18:18:56:538:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:last term reflects a pecuniary externality that operates through the wage and is positive as
29:995:63508:18:18:56:538:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:long ascTis below its first-best levelcT,G.  WhenMis large enough,  the marginal gains
29:996:63594:18:18:56:539:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the region aboveKmore than offset the marginal losses in the region belowK, and the
29:997:63680:18:18:56:538:171:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:government’s optimal response is to intervene.  The caseM=M′′in panel (b) of Figure3
29:998:63764:18:18:56:538:153:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is an example in which fiscal capacity is high enough that the optimal policy is maximal
29:999:63852:18:21:56:124:135:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intervention.
29:1000:63865:21:18:70:538:114:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Notice the difference between private and social incentives. Private consumers could also
29:1001:63954:18:0:56:538:96:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be given the option to make a unilateral transfer to banks, but they would never choose to
30:1002:64046:0:18:56:538:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:make it.  The crucial difference between the government and individual consumers is that
30:1003:64134:18:18:56:538:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the government internalizes the general equilibrium effects of higher investment on wages.
30:1004:64224:18:21:56:438:700:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:As the argument above shows, this is what makes intervention optimal.
30:1005:64293:21:18:70:538:679:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Having studied the best response of the government, we can now characterize the equi-
30:1006:64378:18:30:56:321:661:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:libria in the model with government intervention.
30:1007:64427:30:33:56:188:631:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:C:Proposition 7.Let MBbe
30:1008:64449:33:33:196:538:598:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:MB=nB1+ξ(1−α)Kα1+βξ(1−α)Kα.(25)
30:1009:64480:33:18:56:538:565:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:The economy with government intervention has a unique continuation equilibrium if and only if
30:1010:64573:18:18:57:538:547:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:MB>ˆM and the allocation corresponds to the good continuation equilibrium with no government
30:1011:64665:18:18:56:538:529:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:intervention.  If  MB≤ˆM, there are at least two stable continuation equilibria:  one with K2=K
30:1012:64760:18:33:56:169:511:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:and one with K2=K∗.
30:1013:64779:33:18:70:538:478:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Let  the  functionsN(M,n1)andM(M,n1)denote  the  values  ofMandn1that  come
30:1014:64854:18:18:56:539:460:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from  (23)-(24)  after  substituting  the  government’s  optimal  responses  to{n1,M}on  the
30:1015:64946:18:18:56:538:442:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:right-hand side.  An equilibrium corresponds to a fixed point of the functionN ×M, that
30:1016:65033:18:19:56:99:424:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is a pair
30:1017:65042:19:26:204:390:405:12:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f3:A:{n1,M}={N(M,n1),M(M,n1)}.
30:1018:65067:26:33:56:321:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Also, similar to the definition ofMB, let us define
30:1019:65118:33:36:187:408:346:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:MG=nG1+ξ(1−α)Kα1+βξ(1−α)(K∗)α.
30:1020:65148:36:18:70:538:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To  illustrate  Proposition7  graphically,  we  plotM(M,n1)in  Figure4,  fixingn1at  its
30:1021:65236:18:18:56:538:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bad equilibrium levelnB1.  It is easy to show thatMis non-decreasing in its first argument
30:1022:65326:18:18:56:538:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:because  Proposition6  shows  that  a  larger  capacity  to  intervene  leads  the  government  to
30:1023:65424:18:18:56:538:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:choose  weakly  higher  levels  forK2andcT.   Now  two  cases  are  possible.   In  panel  (a)  of
30:1024:65522:18:18:56:538:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the figure,  we show the caseMB<ˆM.  In this case,  the bad equilibrium survives under
30:1025:65608:18:18:56:538:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:government intervention because, under pessimistic expectations about future wages, the
30:1026:65695:18:18:56:538:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:government has insufficient fiscal resources to intervene. And low investment validates the
30:1027:65786:18:18:56:538:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:private sector’s expectations by keeping future wages low. This is represented by pointCin
30:1028:65876:18:18:56:538:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the figure.  At the same time, the good equilibrium (pointAin the figure) is also possible.
30:1029:65967:18:18:56:538:148:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:To complete the argument for the existence of the good equilibrium, we just need to note
30:1030:66055:18:18:56:538:130:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that if the government chooses to intervene, the constraintk2≥n1/(1−βθ)is not binding,
30:1031:66141:18:21:56:255:112:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:soM(MG,nG1) =M(MG,nB1) =MG.
30:1032:66168:21:0:70:538:91:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In panel (b) of Figure4, we show the caseMB>ˆM.  In this case, the bad equilibrium
31:1033:66252:0:28:142:453:534:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:(a)  Multiplicity(b)  Uniqueness
31:1034:66284:28:34:164:431:506:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 4: Equilibria with government intervention
31:1035:66333:34:18:56:538:472:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the economy with no intervention is ruled out because if we start there, the government
31:1036:66423:18:19:56:538:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:has sufficient resources to move the economy to a better allocation. In fact, this condition is
31:1037:66518:19:18:56:538:435:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sufficient to rule out any equilibrium that does not correspond to the good equilibrium with
31:1038:66610:18:18:56:538:417:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:no intervention. Again, the full argument relies on the fact that the value ofn1/(1−βθ)as
31:1039:66699:18:18:56:538:399:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a lower bound fork2is irrelevant if the government finds it optimal to intervene and go to
31:1040:66789:18:43:56:216:381:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the upper boundM/(1−βθ).
31:1041:66813:43:29:56:161:338:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:5.4    Discussion
31:1042:66830:29:21:56:538:309:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Let us add a few remarks on the assumptions made in modeling government intervention.
31:1043:66915:21:18:70:538:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:First,  in  our  simple  model,  the  government  has  no  incentive  to  intervene  in  a  neigh-
31:1044:67013:18:19:56:538:270:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:borhood of the bad equilibrium.  This is a useful simplification that comes from the way
31:1045:67101:19:18:56:538:251:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we model the inferior technology.  It is possible to enrich the model in order to make the
31:1046:67191:18:18:56:538:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:decision problem of the government smoother, either by introducing richer tax distortions
31:1047:67280:18:18:56:538:215:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(e.g., via a labor supply margin) or by complicating our model of capital accumulation not
31:1048:67370:18:18:56:538:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financed by banks.  This could eliminate the non-convexity in the government’s problem
31:1049:67456:18:18:56:538:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and also make some level of intervention optimal in the bad equilibrium. The crucial thing
31:1050:67546:18:18:56:538:161:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is to have some force that makes the slope of the mapMrelatively low near the bad equi-
31:1051:67633:18:18:56:538:143:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:librium, so that government intervention near the bad equilibrium is not powerful enough
31:1052:67721:18:21:56:418:125:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to push the economy to uniquely converge to the good equilibrium.
31:1053:67786:21:18:70:538:104:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Second, let us discuss the role of our timing assumptions.  Market clearing in the non-
31:1054:67873:18:0:56:538:86:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tradable  goods  market  and  government  borrowing  happen  in  the  first  subperiod.   This
32:1055:67969:0:18:56:539:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implies  that  the  banks’  net  worth—which  depends  onp1—and  the  government  borrow-
32:1056:68058:18:18:56:538:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing  capacity  are  determined  by  consumers’  expectations  regarding  future  wages,  which
32:1057:68152:18:18:56:538:700:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:depend  on  their  expectations  aboutK2.   When  the  government  intervenes  in  the  second
32:1058:68246:18:18:56:538:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:subperiod, the variablesn1andMhave already been determined, so the government must
32:1059:68328:18:18:56:539:664:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:take them as given even though its interventions will affectK2.  If the model featured the
32:1060:68418:18:18:56:538:646:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simultaneous determination of government policy and ofwe2andp1, then it would be easy
32:1061:68503:18:30:56:463:628:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the government to rule out multiplicity, as shown in the following result.
32:1062:68581:30:19:56:538:598:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:C:Proposition 8.Consider the model with government intervention, but assume that the actions in
32:1063:68674:19:18:56:538:579:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:the first and second subperiods are simultaneous.  Then, the government can uniquely implement
32:1064:68768:18:32:56:317:561:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:the first-best allocation. This holds true even ifξ=0.
32:1065:68822:32:19:70:538:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The logic for this result is that a successful lender of last resort is fully self-financed.  If
32:1066:68918:19:18:56:538:510:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  government  makes  a  large  enough  transfer  to  banks,  investment  goes  up  and  future
32:1067:69015:18:18:56:538:492:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wage  expectations  increase,  and  this  raises  demand  on  the  non-tradable  market,  leading
32:1068:69112:18:18:56:538:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to an appreciation.  Then banks’ net worth increases, allowing banks to finance the higher
32:1069:69202:18:18:56:538:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:investment level and creating sufficient collateral to repay the government transfer in full.
32:1070:69295:18:18:56:538:438:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:So if everything is simultaneous, the government can switch to the good equilibrium allo-
32:1071:69384:18:21:56:278:420:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cation by making a large enough transfer.
32:1072:69425:21:18:70:538:399:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To meaningfully discuss the relation between fiscal capacity and lending of last resort,
32:1073:69513:18:18:56:538:381:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we need a model that breaks the simultaneity of Proposition8.  Our timing offers a simple
32:1074:69602:18:18:56:538:363:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:way to break the simultaneity. An open area for future research is to explore richer dynamic
32:1075:69694:18:18:56:538:345:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:specifications that capture more realistically the back and forth between government actions
32:1076:69786:18:50:56:286:327:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and market responses in this type of setup.
32:1077:69829:50:34:56:238:277:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:6    The role of reserves
32:1078:69854:34:18:56:538:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We now consider the role of foreign currency reserves. To do so, we allow the government
32:1079:69942:18:18:56:538:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to take positions in tradable and non-tradable bonds at date 0,  so the government enters
32:1080:70031:18:18:56:538:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period 1 with an initial financial positionAT1+p1AN1.  The analysis of the previous section
32:1081:70122:18:18:56:538:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can easily be extended to this case. However, in order to proceed, we need to make assump-
32:1082:70212:18:18:56:538:171:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions on how the economy responds at date 0 to the portfolio choices of the government.
32:1083:70299:18:21:56:244:153:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Here we consider two experiments.
32:1084:70332:21:18:70:538:132:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:First,  we  consider  the  case  of  unexpected  interventions.   That  is,  we  assume  the  gov-
32:1085:70430:18:18:56:538:114:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ernment buys the portfolio(AT1,AN1)at date 0, but the private sector does not expect the
32:1086:70518:18:0:56:538:96:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:government to use these resources to intervene in financial markets.  Second, we consider
33:1087:70609:0:18:56:538:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the case of fully anticipated interventions.  That is, we assume that the private sector takes
33:1088:70703:18:18:56:538:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:into  account  that  the  government  will  use  its  resources  to  intervene  optimally  at  date  1.
33:1089:70806:18:44:56:537:700:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Both exercises are useful in understanding how reserve accumulation affects the economy.
33:1090:70894:44:29:56:257:656:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:6.1    Unexpected interventions
33:1091:70925:29:18:56:538:627:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In our first experiment, we assume that the private sector expects the government to simply
33:1092:71016:18:18:56:538:609:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:transferAT1+p1AN1back  to  the  consumers  at  date  1.   This  experiment  shows  how  the
33:1093:71107:18:21:56:538:591:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:portfolio(AT1,AN1)changes the government’s ability to credibly act as a lender of last resort.
33:1094:71201:21:18:70:538:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For this experiment, we need to move in two steps. First, we characterize the equilibrium
33:1095:71290:18:18:56:538:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in which the government buys the portfolio(AT1,AN1)at date 0 but doesnotintervene in
33:1096:71374:18:18:56:538:534:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial markets at date 1. This step gives us agents’ portfolios at date 0. Then, given these
33:1097:71469:18:21:56:453:516:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:portfolios, we will study “off-equilibrium” optimal interventions at date 1.
33:1098:71545:21:18:70:538:495:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Suppose  we  start  at  the  fragile  equilibrium  of  an  economy  with  no  government  inter-
33:1099:71641:18:18:56:538:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vention and a zero government portfolio.  If the government buys(AT1,AN1)at date 0 and
33:1100:71727:18:18:56:538:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:transfers the net return back to the consumers at date 1, it is easy to see that there is still a
33:1101:71824:18:19:56:538:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fragile equilibrium, with values ofaT1+AT1andaN1+AN1identical to those of the original
33:1102:71910:19:18:56:538:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium.  All remaining quantities and prices are unchanged.  This is a standard Ricar-
33:1103:72001:18:18:56:538:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dian  equivalence  result.  The  only  thing  we  need  to  check,  given  that  taxes  are  bounded
33:1104:72101:18:18:56:538:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by  (17),  is  that  the  government  has  sufficient  fiscal  capacity  to  finance  the  net  value  of
33:1105:72206:18:21:56:480:368:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:(AT1,AN1)in all states of the world. We will take care of this requirement below.
33:1106:72287:21:18:70:538:347:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We can then turn to the off-equilibrium analysis of interventions at date 1.  The analysis
33:1107:72377:18:18:56:538:329:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the previous section can easily be extended to the case in which the government enters
33:1108:72466:18:18:56:538:311:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period 1 with a non-zero portfolio(AT1,AN1).  Only two things change.  First, the definition
33:1109:72558:18:33:56:320:293:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the total resources available to banksMis now
33:1110:72606:33:33:163:432:260:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:M=AT1+p1AN1+n1+ξ(1−α)Kα1+βξ(1−α)Kα2.
33:1111:72642:33:33:56:520:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Second, the resource constraint (19) in the government maximization problem becomes
33:1112:72725:33:33:128:467:194:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:(1+β)cT+βcTb≤aT1+AT1−bT1+Kα1+βKα2−k2−φ(K2−k2).
33:1113:72771:33:18:56:538:161:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:However,  we  just  made  the  argument  that,  in  the  case  of  unexpected  interventions,  the
33:1114:72869:18:18:56:538:143:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium value ofaT1+AT1will be the same asaT1in the economy with a zero government
33:1115:72955:18:21:56:454:125:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:portfolio. Therefore, the government maximization problem is unchanged.
33:1116:73026:21:18:70:538:104:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  fact  that  the  maximization  problem  of  the  government  is  unchanged  implies  that
33:1117:73120:18:0:56:539:86:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the cutoffˆMis equivalent to the case withAT1=AN1studied in Proposition 6. We can then
34:1118:73208:0:30:56:200:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:derive the following result.
34:1119:73236:30:18:56:538:706:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:C:Proposition  9.Take  an  economy  with  a  fragile  equilibrium.   LetˆM  and  MBbe  defined  as  in
34:1120:73336:18:33:56:435:688:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:Propositions 6and7. Suppose the portfolio(AT1,AN1)satisfies the inequalities
34:1121:73412:33:21:133:538:655:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:AT1+pB1AN1>ˆM−MB,(26)
34:1122:73433:21:21:132:538:634:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:AT1+pG1AN1>−ξ(1−α)[Kα1+β(K∗)α],(27)
34:1123:73468:21:33:119:538:613:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:qT0AT1+qN0AN1<βE[AT1+p1AN1] +ξ(1−α)E[Kα0+βKα1+β2Kα2].(28)
34:1124:73525:33:18:56:538:580:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:Then, given the positions(AT1,AN1), the good equilibrium is the unique continuation equilibrium
34:1125:73620:18:33:56:205:562:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:with government intervention.
34:1126:73649:33:16:70:538:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f10:A:To provide an interpretation of this result, consider the interesting case in whichMB<
34:1127:73735:16:20:61:538:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:ˆM,  so optimal government intervention withAT1=AN1=0 is not sufficient to eliminate
34:1128:73819:20:21:56:310:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the bad equilibrium, as shown in Proposition7.
34:1129:73865:21:18:70:538:472:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Now  suppose  the  government  borrows  in  non-tradables  to  finance  the  accumulation
34:1130:73954:18:18:56:538:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  reserves  denominated  in  tradables,  taking  positionsAT1>0>AN1,  and  assume  that
34:1131:74043:18:18:56:538:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these positions yield a zero average payoffE[AT1+p1AN1] =0.  Given thatpG1>pB1,  the
34:1132:74127:18:19:56:538:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:government makes a net gain in the bad state and a net loss in the good state.  Moreover,
34:1133:74216:19:18:56:538:399:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:given that tradable bonds pay a lower expected return than non-tradable bonds in a fragile
34:1134:74306:18:21:56:393:381:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium, the portfolio will costqT0AT1+qN0AN1>0 at date 0.
34:1135:74368:21:18:70:538:360:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Condition  (26)  ensures  that  the  net  portfolio  gain  in  the  bad  state  is  large  enough  to
34:1136:74469:18:18:56:538:342:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cover the differenceˆM−MB. This shifts up the resources available in the bad equilibrium,
34:1137:74558:18:18:56:538:324:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:moving  us  from  the  situation  depicted  in  panel  (a)  of  Figure4  to  the  situation  depicted
34:1138:74659:18:18:56:538:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in panel (b), and thus eliminating the bad equilibrium.  This is our main result on the ex
34:1139:74749:18:18:56:538:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:post effects of reserve accumulation:  reserves allow the government to hedge against the
34:1140:74838:18:18:56:538:270:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bad  equilibrium  state  and,  by  boosting  the  government’s  resources  in  that  state,  end  up
34:1141:74938:18:21:56:219:252:12:g_d0_f3:9:g_d0_f3:B:eliminating that equilibrium.18
34:1142:74969:21:18:70:538:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The results above provide a rationale for some recent empirical findings.Obstfeld, Sham-
34:1143:75057:18:18:56:538:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:baugh, and Taylor(2010) show that the size of the banking sector liabilities is an important
34:1144:75149:18:18:56:538:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:predictor in explaining the accumulation of foreign currency reserves by emerging markets.
34:1145:75239:18:18:56:538:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In our model, we can compare two economies that have multiple equilibria atKandK∗,
34:1146:75321:18:20:56:538:159:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have the same foreign net positionaT1−bT1, and are identical in all other respects except for
34:1147:75414:20:7:69:402:139:8:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f4:F:18Conditions (27) and (28) are needed to make sure that the portfolio(AT
34:1148:75486:7:0:397:414:132:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f4:F:1,A
34:1149:75489:0:7:415:421:139:8:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:F:N
34:1150:75490:7:9:414:538:132:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:1)is feasible.  In particular,
34:1151:75520:9:12:56:538:123:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:condition (27) ensures that the government has sufficient fiscal capacity to cover the portfolio losses in the
34:1152:75630:12:11:56:538:111:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:good  state.   Condition  (28)  ensures  that  it  has  sufficient  fiscal  capacity  to  cover  the  ex  ante  cost  of  reserve
34:1153:75759:11:0:56:118:100:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:accumulation.
35:1154:75774:0:18:56:538:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the balance sheet of the financial sector at date 1, that is, for the debt levelsbN1andbT1. The
35:1155:75869:18:30:56:321:718:12:g_d0_f3:9:g_d0_f3:B:conditions in Proposition9 imply the following:19
35:1156:75918:30:18:56:539:688:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:C:Remark 1(Reserves and banks’ balance sheets).Between the two economies described above,
35:1157:76005:18:33:56:493:670:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:the one with more bank debt requires a higher value of AT1to rule out the bad equilibrium.
35:1158:76095:33:18:70:538:637:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Leverage  in  the  banking  sector  reduces  banks’  net  worth  in  a  crisis,  thus  requiring  a
35:1159:76194:18:21:56:369:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:larger government buffer to eliminate the bad equilibrium.
35:1160:76252:21:30:70:304:598:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A second remark comes out of our analysis.
35:1161:76294:30:18:56:538:568:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:C:Remark  2(Unused  reserves).Reserves  can  play  a  useful  role  in  credibly  ruling  out  financial
35:1162:76396:18:33:56:270:550:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:panics and yet never be used in equilibrium.
35:1163:76440:33:18:70:538:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:When  the  conditions  in  Proposition9  are  satisfied,  the  government  doesn’t  intervene
35:1164:76533:18:18:56:538:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in equilibrium and rebates the reserves back to the households.  However, the presence of
35:1165:76622:18:18:56:538:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reserves is important to rule out the bad equilibrium.  This remark connects our analysis
35:1166:76711:18:18:56:538:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  another  empirical  observation:   emerging  markets  seem  to  hold  on  to  their  stocks  of
35:1167:76810:18:18:56:538:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reserves, even in times of distress.Aizenman and Sun(2012) provide evidence of this type
35:1168:76898:18:18:56:538:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of behavior—which they dub “fear of losing international reserves”—looking at emerging
35:1169:76984:18:44:56:337:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economies’ response to the global downturn of 2009.
35:1170:77035:44:29:56:257:365:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:6.2    Anticipated interventions
35:1171:77067:29:18:56:538:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We now consider the case of a fully expected intervention, that is, we assume that agents
35:1172:77156:18:18:56:538:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:correctly anticipate that the government will use reserves optimally att=1 to eliminate
35:1173:77243:18:21:56:165:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the bad equilibrium.
35:1174:77263:21:18:70:538:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Suppose, in particular, that we start at a fragile equilibrium and the government takes
35:1175:77350:18:19:56:538:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:positions that satisfy the conditions in Proposition9.  If all agents correctly anticipate that
35:1176:77445:19:18:56:538:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the government will intervene and eliminate the bad equilibrium, the positions they take at
35:1177:77536:18:18:56:538:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:date 0 will adjust. In particular, it is possible to show that there is an equilibrium in which
35:1178:77631:18:18:56:538:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the values ofbT1−AT1andbN1−AN1are equal to the values ofbT1andbN1in the safe equi-
35:1179:77713:18:18:56:538:188:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:librium constructed in Proposition5 and the conditions of Proposition9 are satisfied,  so
35:1180:77802:18:18:56:538:170:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:there is a unique (good) continuation equilibrium. This means that the consolidated dollar
35:1181:77892:18:18:56:538:152:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:debt of the banks and the government is lower, and their consolidated peso debt is larger
35:1182:77981:18:19:56:538:134:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relative to the original fragile equilibrium. In other words, increased dollar holdings by the
35:1183:78075:19:16:69:538:115:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:19Notice  that  the  value  ofˆMdepends  on  the  net  foreign  position  of  the  country,  but  not  on  individual
35:1184:78192:16:0:56:122:99:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:balance sheets.
36:1185:78209:0:18:56:538:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:government are not undone by increased dollar borrowing by the banks.  We summarize
36:1186:78292:18:30:56:222:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this finding in the next remark.
36:1187:78324:30:18:56:538:688:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f4:C:Remark 3(Catalytic reserves).When reserves are large enough to eliminate the bad equilibrium,
36:1188:78417:18:33:56:521:670:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f4:C:their presence can lead to a higher net consolidated dollar position of banks and the government.
36:1189:78514:33:18:70:538:637:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Here the interesting observation is that banks do not have incentives to undo the positive
36:1190:78604:18:18:56:538:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:foreign  currency  position  of  the  government  by  borrowing  more  in  foreign  currency.   In
36:1191:78702:18:18:56:538:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:other words, the presence of credible intervention at datet=1 does not induce more risk
36:1192:78789:18:18:56:539:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:taking by banks att=0 as the usual moral hazard logic would suggest, and anticipated
36:1193:78873:18:21:56:335:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:government rescues do not lead to more risk taking.
36:1194:78924:21:18:70:538:544:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To understand the logic behind this result, it is useful to identify two opposing channels
36:1195:79014:18:21:56:440:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:through which government intervention affects banks’ behavior ex ante.
36:1196:79084:21:18:70:538:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:First, if we fix the interest rates in tradables and non-tradables at date 0, there is a direct
36:1197:79179:18:18:56:538:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect  of  intervention  that  leads  banks  to  issue  more  tradable  debt.   The  argument  is  as
36:1198:79281:18:19:56:538:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:follows.  As argued in Section4, the presence of the bad equilibrium gives banks an incen-
36:1199:79371:19:18:56:538:450:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tive to borrow less in tradables, as the marginal value of net worth is higher and tradable
36:1200:79462:18:18:56:538:432:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:debt  increases  in  value  in  the  bad  equilibrium.   Therefore,  when  the  bad  equilibrium  is
36:1201:79562:18:18:56:538:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:removed, the incentive to borrow in tradables goes up. This is the traditional moral hazard
36:1202:79653:18:18:56:538:396:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mechanism, where reducing the risk to which banks are exposed (by eliminating the bad
36:1203:79738:18:21:56:317:378:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equilibrium) would lead to increased risk taking.
36:1204:79787:21:18:70:538:357:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Second, there is a general equilibrium effect that works in the opposite direction. When
36:1205:79875:18:18:56:538:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:government interventions remove the bad equilibrium, domestic savers are no longer con-
36:1206:79962:18:18:56:538:321:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cerned about a large depreciation correlated to a contraction in consumption. Hence, savers
36:1207:80053:18:18:56:538:303:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will demand more non-tradable denominated assets.  This force pushes down the interest
36:1208:80139:18:18:56:538:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate differential between tradable and non-tradable denominated debt and induces banks
36:1209:80225:18:21:56:233:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to borrow more in non-tradables.
36:1210:80257:21:18:70:538:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our argument above shows that the general equilibrium effect dominates in our econ-
36:1211:80340:18:50:56:81:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:omy.
36:1212:80344:50:34:56:172:178:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:7    Conclusion
36:1213:80359:34:18:56:538:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Our  model  provides  a  novel  perspective  on  financial  dollarization  in  emerging  markets,
36:1214:80456:18:18:56:538:126:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pointing out the interaction between financial instability and the precautionary motive of
36:1215:80546:18:18:56:538:108:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:domestic savers. We have used our model to study the ex post and ex ante effects of lending
36:1216:80637:18:0:56:538:90:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of last resort, introducing a notion of fiscally credible interventions.  Our analysis provides
37:1217:80734:0:18:56:538:736:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a rationale for the view that official foreign currency reserves support financial stability, as
37:1218:80830:18:21:56:500:718:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:they improve the credibility of domestic authorities to intervene in financial panics.
37:1219:80916:21:21:70:512:697:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our model is very stylized and abstracts from a numer of interesting policy issues.
37:1220:80999:21:18:70:538:676:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:First,  we  leave  aside  the  role  of  monetary  policy.   Our  model  can  be  interpreted  as
37:1221:81096:18:18:56:538:658:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:making  the  implicit  assumption  that  the  domestic  monetary  authority  is  committed  to
37:1222:81190:18:18:56:538:640:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:keep the price of non-tradables stable. It would be interesting to model explicitly monetary
37:1223:81282:18:18:56:538:622:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:policy  in  an  environment  with  nominal  rigidities,  to  capture  important  dilemmas  faced
37:1224:81378:18:18:56:538:604:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by monetary policy both ex post and ex ante.  Ex post,  the monetary authority faces the
37:1225:81466:18:18:56:538:586:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:problem  that  a  monetary  expansion  causes  a  nominal  devaluation,  which  increases  the
37:1226:81560:18:18:56:538:568:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:burden of dollar debt. Ex ante, the monetary authority faces the problem that agents taking
37:1227:81651:18:19:56:538:550:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:domestic currency positions are afraid of future inflation in financial crises. We leave these
37:1228:81745:19:20:56:188:531:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:issues to future research.
37:1229:81771:20:19:70:538:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Second, in our paper, the role of foreign currency reserves is to boost the fiscal position
37:1230:81862:19:18:56:538:492:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the domestic government in the event of a crisis.  There are additional reasons why dol-
37:1231:81953:18:18:56:538:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lar reserves can help support a financial system in distress.  In particular, currency market
37:1232:82046:18:18:56:538:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interventions can be used to dampen movements in the exchange rate, reducing the bur-
37:1233:82131:18:18:56:538:438:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:den of foreign currency debt.20Capturing this role would require introducing additional
37:1234:82218:18:21:56:470:420:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:frictions in currency markets, which is outside the scope of the present paper.
37:1235:82297:21:18:70:538:399:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The central mechanism of our paper is that private savers do not internalize the effect
37:1236:82384:18:18:56:538:381:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of their portfolio choices on the financial fragility of the economy. The logic of this mecha-
37:1237:82478:18:18:56:538:363:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nism can be extended beyond the specific environment considered here, where savers only
37:1238:82565:18:18:56:538:345:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:choose the currency composition of their portfolio. In ongoing work, we explore this mech-
37:1239:82655:18:18:56:538:327:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:anism in a more general dynamic macro-financial model in which borrowers and lenders
37:1240:82739:18:207:56:480:309:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:trade state contingent claims, and study its implications for aggregate volatility.
37:1241:82822:207:16:69:538:102:8:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:20Ilzetzki, Reinhart, and Rogoff(2017) interpret reserve accumulation by emerging economies as a tool to
37:1242:82926:16:0:56:193:86:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f3:F:reduce exchange rate volatility.

52:1854:105161:21:18:70:538:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We can start by deriving an intertemporal resource constraint for the economy by con-
